- Prypco Mint Terms & Conditions — https://prypco.com/mint/terms-and-conditions
- Prypco Blocks Terms & Conditions — https://prypco.com/blocks/terms-and-conditions
- Prypco Broker-Dealer Disclosure — https://prypco.com/mint/broker-dealer-disclosure

# Terms and Conditions

Scroll Progress 0%

##### 1\. INTRODUCTION

1.1. This Agreement governs the contractual relationship on which we, PRYPCO Mint (trading name PRYPCO FZE) (“PRYPCO, us or we”), enable you to invest in properties available on our Platform [(https://mint.prypco.com)](https://mint.prypco.com/)(the “Platform”). Please read this Agreement carefully before using our Platform.

1.2. PRYPCO FZE, is a company incorporated and registered in the Dubai World Trade Centre with company registration number L-2048 whose registered address is at 04, Sheikh Rashid Tower, Dubai World Trade Centre (Premise No: FZH 378 SRT) and is authorised and licensed by the Dubai Virtual Assets Regulatory Authority (“VARA”), for the purpose of broker dealer activities under VARA licence number, VL/25/05/001

1.3. PRYPCO FZE is a wholly owned subsidiary ultimately owned by PRYPCO Holding Limited, a company incorporated and registered in DIFC whose registered office is at Tower A, 314, DAMAC Park Towers, DIFC, Dubai, UAE.

1.4. By continuing to use the Platform, you agree to be bound by the terms and conditions set out in this Agreement together with the:

- [Terms and Conditions (https://mint.prypco.com/tnc)](https://mint.prypco.com/tnc)

- [Cookies Policy (https://mint.prypco.com/cookie-policy)](https://mint.prypco.com/cookie-policy)

- [Privacy Statement (https://mint.prypco.com/privacy-statement)](https://mint.prypco.com/privacy-statement)

- [Third Party Service Providers (https://mint.prypco.com/third-party-providers)](https://mint.prypco.com/third-party-providers)


1.5. Further, you agree and acknowledge that you have read and understood the Key Risks and Disclosure on our Platform. This Agreement will come into effect upon you confirming electronically on the Platform that you agree to them. A copy of this Agreement will be provided upon acceptance of the terms on our Platform.

## 2\. DEFINITIONS

2.1. “Client Money Account” means a standalone bank account with Zand Bank P.J.S.C designed to securely hold funds separately from PRYPCO FZE’s operational finances. This segregation ensures the distinct separation of client funds, minimising the risk of misuse or misappropriation and prioritizing the safety and protection of clients' assets.

2.2. “Commitment Period” means a period commencing from the time you have invested in the Property through the Platform until the Property has been transferred from the Seller to you.

2.3. “Cooling Off Period” refers to a period consisting of the first 24 hours after you invest in a Property.

2.4. “Dividend” refers to the periodic income generated by the Investment less any fees or costs.

2.5. “Funding Target” refers to the investment required to acquire the Property including, without limitations, all associated costs as detailed on the Platform.

2.6. “Investment” means the percentage of the Property you own by purchasing, or committing to purchase a fraction of the Property through PRYPCO FZE. In return, PRYPCO FZE will use the funds raised to acquire the subject Property on your behalf and you will hold title to the subject Property for the Investment Term.

2.7. “Investment Round” refers to a defined period detailed on the Platform during which the fundraising activities are carried out and remain in progress to achieve the Funding Target.

2.8. “Investment Term” refers to a period commencing from the date when you acquire the Property until such Property is sold either upon the expiry of the investment period or, early sale of the Property by majority vote of the Investors or upon operation of the law.

2.9. “KYC and AML” means all the applicable measures, processes and techniques used for Know Your Customer (KYC) and Anti-Money Laundering (AML) purposes to identify an investor or potential investor and his/her source of funds amongst other requirements, as may change from time to time at our sole discretion, in accordance with our KYC and AML Policy.

2.10. “Lock in Period” means the three (3) month period from the date of the Investment Term. Within this period, Investors cannot sell their share of the Property they own.

2.11. “Material Change” means any change or new matter that may significantly affect the value of the Property, the ability of the Property to be rented, return on the Property or the value of the Investment.

2.12. “Platform Documents” refers to all disclosures, information, agreements, terms and conditions and policies made available on the Platform, including but not limited to the Platform General Terms of Use and Data and Privacy Policy.

2.13. “Property” means a building, apartment, villa or residential house identified for investment or acquired via PRYPCO FZE on behalf of the investors for the Investment.

2.14. “Property Valuation” refers to the systematic process of determining the monetary value of a real estate asset. This assessment involves the analysis of various factors, including location, size, condition, amenities, and recent comparable sales in the area.

2.15. “PRYPCO Wallet” refers to the funds held in the Client Money Account pertaining to the customer.

2.16. “PRYPCO Account” refers to a user account created on the Platform showing PRYPCO Wallets and such other personalised features to be used by you to make investments and receive and manage funds in addition to monitoring and managing other matters relevant to your Investments.

2.17. “ROI” means the return on investment on a Property over the Investment Term, calculated as the total net income earned from all Dividend distributions and capital appreciation (as measured by the latest periodic property valuation) divided by the purchase price of the Property.

2.18. “Reserve Funds” is an amount deducted at the start of the Investment and kept as an ongoing allowance to pay for any maintenance charges that may arise in relation to the Property.

2.19. “Sale Value” refers to the gross proceeds of sale received from a buyer of the Property at the end of the Investment Term or the gross proceeds of sale received from a buyer to purchase an Investors portion of the Property listed on our Platform at point of exit.

2.20. “Seller” means the individual or company that owns the legal Title Deed to the Property prior to the Investment Term.

2.21. “Title Deed” is a legal document that serves as evidence of ownership or interest in a property.

2.22. “Trust Account” is a bank account held in the name of the Dubai Land Department (“DLD”) for the purpose of holding governmental fees prior to property transfer, at which point the funds will be transferred directly to DLD.

2.23. “You”, “your” and “Investors” refers to current or potential investors of a Property.

## 3\. GENERAL

3.1. The Platform is developed and managed by PRYPCO Real Estate LLC and provides details of each Property available for investment. Our role is to facilitate the purchase of fractionalised properties for sale to prospective investors through the Platform. Individual Investors will own a direct portion of the Property proportional to their investment, subject to the terms of this Agreement. The ownership of the property will be held in tokenized format. These tokens are issued by DLD and minted by DLD’s tokenization engine, Ctrl Alt Solutions DMCC and held in a warm multi party computation omnibus account, with Ctrl Alt Solutions DMCC as the custodian. For the avoidance of doubt, and subject to clause 18 Limitation of Liability and 19 Indemnity, PRYPCO remains responsible for all Investor virtual assets.

3.2. We will start an Investment Round through the Platform to pool Investments from potential Investors to secure the Funding Target. Once the Funding Target is achieved, in exchange for the Investment, the Investors will directly own a share of the Property, registered in their name with DLD proportional to their investment amount. The Funding Target will be the price agreed between us and the Seller together with the associated costs incurred as a result of acquiring the Property. Details of all fees pertaining to the Property will be listed on the Platform.

3.3. PRYPCO will verify the sale price using either DLD’s smart valuation or using a leading independent accredited valuer, who will provide a report on the Property.

3.4. Subject to the terms of this Agreement, you understand that your Investment will be used for the acquisition of the Property that you invest in. By investing in a Property, you agree to pay proportional fees and charges associated with the acquisition of the Property and other related costs in connection with the Investment as set out on the Platform. Should you have any query in connection with any provisions of this Agreement and the investment process, you are encouraged to read through the FAQ’s and if in doubt contact us through [support.mint@prypco.com](mailto:support.mint@prypco.com).

3.5. If we fail to achieve the Funding Target within a certain period, the Investment Round will be discontinued and the amount that you invested will be returned to your PRYPCO Wallet in its entirety. No costs, expenses or fees will be deducted from the amount of the Investment, except if the original funds in your PRYPCO Wallet which were used to make the Investment were in a currency different than that of the underlying Investment, in which case charges for foreign exchange may apply or under a promotion run by us, which will be subject to separate terms and conditions. In such a case, you can use the amount refunded back to your PRYPCO Wallet to invest in another Property listed on the Platform. If you choose not to invest in another Property, you can withdraw the funds from your PRYPCO Wallet to the bank account registered with us in the manner stated hereunder, in which case all bank transfer, foreign exchange and other pro

# Broker-Dealer disclosure

Note:

“PRYPCO Mint” is hereby referred to as “PRYPCO FZE”

Scroll Progress 0%

## Disclosure 1

Conflicts of interest can arise in various business and personal contexts. Proactively managing these conflicts is essential to mitigate legal and regulatory risks while upholding our integrity, brand, and reputation. Conflicts of interest can be managed effectively by:

- Understanding what constitutes a conflict of interest; if you have questions, please consult with your manager or the People and Compliance team.

- Acting with integrity in all business activities.

- Considering potential conflicts of interest in all aspects of your work.

- Avoiding any activities, situations, or relationships that could compromise—or appear to compromise—your professional judgment.

- Seeking approval before engaging in any outside business, financial, or personal relationships that may pose a risk of conflict.


To help identify actual, perceived, or potential conflicts of interest, consider the following questions:

- Could I gain personal benefits, now or in the future, that might influence my objectivity?

- Do I hold any personal or professional views that could lead others to reasonably question my impartiality on a specific matter?

- Have I received a gift, benefit, or hospitality from someone who could be affected by my decisions?

- Is there a significant personal, professional, or financial relationship involved?

- Would I, or someone close to me, gain or suffer as a result of my decision or action?

- Could the company’s reputation be positively or negatively impacted by my decision or action?


Proactively considering these questions helps ensure transparency and ethical decision-making across all aspects of our business.

## Disclosure 2

PRYPCO FZE determines the Virtual Assets quotes based on the DLD Smart Valuation Index or through an independent valuation company. These reports are generated every 6 months.

## Disclosure 3

PRYPCO FZE does not hold or maintain funds or Virtual Assets, nor does it provide clearing services for other Virtual Asset Service Providers (VASPs) offering Broker-Dealer services. PRYPCO FZE’s services are focused solely on providing Real World Assets (RWA) fractional ownership access to its customers and do not include custodial or clearing functions for other VASPs.

## Disclosure 4

PRYPCO FZE has implemented robust arrangements to ensure the protection and integrity of clients’ ownership of assets held on the platform. All client assets are securely held in segregated accounts, separate from PRYPCO FZE’s proprietary holdings, to prevent any commingling. Additionally, PRYPCO FZE follows enhanced security measures and regular audits to uphold clients' ownership rights and ensure full compliance with regulatory standards. Clients can access and verify their asset holdings at any time on the PRYPCO FZE platform and on the Dubai REST App, reinforcing our commitment to transparency and asset protection.

## Disclosure 5

PRYPCO FZE may refer or introduce clients to select entities, including other Virtual Asset Service Providers (VASPs), when specific client needs align with services provided by these entities. Such referrals are made transparently, with clients fully informed of the nature and purpose of the introduction. PRYPCO FZE may receive monetary or non-monetary benefits as part of these arrangements, including reciprocation for business referrals, which are disclosed to clients in alignment with regulatory requirements.

# Understanding ARVA tokens: A new era of asset-backed digital ownership

November 25, 2025

![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/cVnBg4Gq2l4bcnZbCRBDdVq0D0.jpg?width=5986&height=3996)

### Understanding ARVA Tokens

Published by:

![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/DwmrN7P6Xuz855NO1jsk1NK6N4o.png?width=279&height=279)

Prateek from PRYPCO

Share articleCopied!Share article

The global investment landscape is evolving, and blockchain-based assets are opening new ways for individuals to participate in real-world value creation. As part of this evolution, Dubai is taking a pioneering role in shaping and regulating the future of tokenized assets.

One of the latest developments in this ecosystem is the introduction of Asset-Referenced Virtual Assets (ARVA), guided by the Virtual Assets Regulatory Authority (VARA).

ARVA tokens are designed to represent rights and benefits linked to real-world assets, offering investors a secure, transparent, and regulated way to participate in asset ownership through digital infrastructure.

# **What are ARVA tokens?**

ARVA tokens are virtual assets that derive their value from real-world assets. They serve as a regulatory-compliant structure for capturing economic and ancillary rights associated with those assets, including income distribution, governance rights, and other entitlements.

Unlike traditional digital tokens that may only represent access or utility, ARVA tokens are linked to the financial characteristics of a real asset. This makes them an important milestone in the journey toward regulated, asset-backed digital ownership.

ARVA tokens are not limited to real estate. They can be applied to multiple asset classes, including:

- Commodities

- Financial instruments

- Yield-generating investments

- Other tangible or reference assets


This flexibility positions ARVAs as a foundation for future growth across the digital asset economy.

### **ARVA tokens in the context of real estate**

In the real estate space, ARVA tokens can represent rights such as:

- Rental income distribution

- Voting rights related to the asset

- Participation in governance decisions

- Other ownership-linked entitlements


For platforms like [PRYPCO Mint](https://mint.prypco.com/?utm_source=organic&utm_medium=blog&utm_campaign=ARVA) that are bringing real estate investment on-chain, ARVA tokens complement title deed tokens and help ensure that investors receive the full economic benefits of property ownership in line with VARA regulations.

This structure supports clarity, transparency, and investor protection while enabling a modern, digital investment experience.

### **A regulatory-first approach**

Dubai continues to lead the global conversation on regulated innovation. VARA's introduction of ARVA tokens reflects a strong commitment to enabling blockchain-based investment models while maintaining a high standard of governance and investor safeguards.

By establishing a clear framework for asset-referenced tokens, VARA is strengthening long-term trust in digital asset markets and encouraging responsible adoption across industries.

This regulatory clarity is helping to build a secure and credible foundation for the future of tokenization in Dubai and beyond.

### **What ARVAs mean for investors?**

For investors, ARVA tokens bring several key advantages:

- **Greater transparency** around entitlements and rights

- **Structured regulatory oversight** for added security

- **Efficient and digital-first ownership experience**

- **Ability to participate in real-world assets** through blockchain infrastructure


As markets evolve, ARVA tokens represent a meaningful step toward broader accessibility and more efficient global investment participation.

### **How will ARVA tokens impact PRYPCO Mint investors?**

**Two Tokens, One Unified Ecosystem** To ensure full compliance with VARA’s new framework while maintaining continuity for our early investors, PRYPCO Mint will now operate with **two interconnected tokens**:

- **Existing Properties:**

Your original title deed tokens from the pilot phase will coexist with ARVA tokens. To align them with VARA’s new standards, we will issue an ARVA Token that is directly linked to each existing tokenized property. This ensures your investment continues to be recognised under the updated regulatory structure without any action required on your part.

- **Upcoming Properties:**

All upcoming listings on [PRYPCO Mint](https://mint.prypco.com/?utm_source=organic&utm_medium=blog&utm_campaign=ARVA) will launch with both tokens from the outset — a title deed token representing the legal ownership of the property and an ARVA Token reflecting the regulated digital asset under VARA’s framework. Together, they provide the most transparent, secure, and compliant structure for real estate investment in the region.


### **Looking ahead**

ARVA tokens mark a significant milestone in the scaling of tokenized real asset investments. Their introduction aligns technological innovation with regulatory progress, building a foundation for long-term adoption and trust.

As Dubai continues shaping the future of real-world asset tokenization, ARVA tokens will play an important role in enabling secure, transparent, and investor-focused digital asset markets across multiple industries.

Whether in real estate or other asset classes, ARVAs are opening the door to a future where ownership becomes more accessible, more efficient, and more globally connected.

Disclaimer: This content is not an offer or solicitation to buy, sell, or hold virtual assets. Virtual assets are subject to market fluctuations, and investors may lose the full value of their investment. No financial protection applies. Please seek independent advice and review the Terms and Conditions before making any investment decision.

# Terms and Conditions

Scroll Progress 0%

###### 1\. INTRODUCTION

1.1.Please read this investment agreement (hereinafter as **"Agreement"**) carefully as it sets out the terms and conditions which permit you to use our website and enable you to make investments in properties using our website, [https://prypco.com/blocks/](https://prypco.com/blocks)(the " **Platform**"). By using the Platform, you agree to be bound by the terms and conditions set out in this Agreement.

1.2.This Agreement governs the contractual relationship between you and PRYPCO Blocks (DIFC) Ltd (" **PRYPCO Blocks**").

1.3.PRYPCO Blocks is authorised and regulated by the Dubai Financial Services Authority (the " **DFSA**") for the purposes of "Operating a Crowdfunding Platform" under DFSA registration number CL7381.

1.4.PRYPCO Blocks (DIFC) Limited is a wholly owned subsidiary of PRYPCO Holdings Limited, a company incorporated and registered in DIFC whose registered office is at Tower A,314, DAMAC Park Towers, DIFC, Dubai, UAE.

1.5.Please note that the Key Risks and Cookies Policy also applies to your general access and use of our Platform for the purpose of investments, and our Privacy Policy applies to our use of your personal information. We recommend that you read these carefully.

1.6.This Agreement will come into effect upon you confirming electronically on the Platform that you agree to them.

1.7.If the Client is classified as a Professional Client pursuant to Clause 2.14 of this Agreement, additional terms and conditions, beyond those set forth in this Agreement, shall be provided to the Client.

###### 2\. DEFINITIONS

2.1. **"Client Money Account"** means a standalone bank account with Emirates NBD (ENBD) designed to securely hold funds separately from PRYPCO Blocks' operational finances. This segregation ensures the distinct separation of client funds, minimising the risk of misuse or misappropriation and prioritizing the safety and protection of clients' assets.

2.2. **"Customer Wallet"** refers to the funds held as cash in the Client Money Account pertaining to the customer.

2.3. **"Commitment Period"** means a period commencing from the time you have committed funds to be invested in the Property through the platform until the purchase transaction is executed, meaning the Property has been transferred from the Seller to the investors.

2.4. **"Cooling Off Period"** refers to a period consisting of the first 48 hours after the property is fully funded.

2.5. **"Dividend"** refers to the periodic income generated by the Investment less any fees or costs.

2.6. **“FTB Investments”** refers to Flip the Blocks Investments. FTB Investments refers to certain investments offered on the Platform involving the acquisition, renovation, refurbishment, and resale of a Property within a shorter-term investment horizon. FTB Investments differ materially from buy-to-hold rental investments and carry additional risks.

**"Funding Target"** refers to the investment required to acquire the Property including, without limitations, all associated costs as detailed on the Platform excluding the PRYPCO fees and the KYC & AML Fee.

2.7. **"Investment Cost"** refers to the total amount payable by the Investor, including, without limitation, the Funding Target, the PRYPCO Acquisition Fee, and the KYC & AML Fee.

2.8. **"Investment"** means an investment amount you made by purchasing, or committing to purchase, the Shares from PRYPCO Blocks which will use the funds raised by the sale of Shares to acquire the subject Property and investors will hold title to the subject Property for a certain Investment Term.

2.9. **"Investment Round"** refers to a defined period detailed on the platform during which the fundraising activities are carried out and remain in progress to achieve the Funding Target.

2.10. **"Investment Term"** refers to a period commencing from the date when the investors acquire Property until such Property is sold either upon the expiry of the investment period, early sale of the Property by majority vote of the Investors or upon operation of the law.

2.11. **"KYC and AML"** means all the applicable measures, processes and techniques used for Know Your Customer (KYC) and Anti-Money Laundering (AML) purposes to identify an Investor or potential Investor and his/her source of funds amongst other requirements, as may change from time to time at our sole discretion, in accordance with our KYC and AML Policy.

2.12. **"Material Change"** means any change or new matter that may significantly affect the value of the Property, the ability of the Property to be rented, return on the Property or the value of the Investment.

2.13. **"Platform Documents"** refers to all disclosures, information, agreements, terms & conditions and policies made available on the platform, including but not limited to the Platform General Terms of Use and Data and Privacy Policy.

2.14. **"Property"** means a building, apartment, villa or residential house identified for investment or acquired via PRYPCO Blocks on behalf of the investors for the Investment.

2.15."Professional Client" is a client who meets the criteria set forth in DFSA Rulebook, Conduct of Business (COB) modules number 2.3.3 and 2.3.4.

2.16."Retail Client" is a client who is not a Professional Client.

2.17. **"ROI"** means the return on investment on a Property over the Investment Term, calculated as the total net income earned from all Dividend distributions and capital appreciation (as measured by the latest periodic property valuation) divided by the purchase price of the Property.

2.18. **"Property Valuation"** refers to the systematic process of determining the monetary value of a real estate asset. This assessment involves the analysis of various factors, including location, size, condition, amenities, and recent comparable sales in the area.

2.19. **"Sale Value"** refers to the gross proceeds of sale received from a buyer of the Property at the end of the Investment Term.

2.20. **"Seller"** means the individual or company that owns the legal title deed to the Property prior to the Investment.

2.21. **"Title Deed"** is a legal document that serves as evidence of ownership or interest in a property.

2.22. **"PRYPCO Blocks"**, **"we"**, **"our"** and **"us"** refer to PRYPCO Blocks (DIFC) Ltd, a company incorporated and registered in the Dubai International Financial Centre (" **DIFC**) with company registration number CL7381. PRYPCO Blocks is authorised and regulated by the Dubai Financial Services Authority (the " **DFSA**) as an Operator of a Property Crowdfunding Platform under DFSA Reference Number F007958.

2.23. **"PRYPCO Blocks Account"** refers to a user account created on the platform showing Customer Wallets and such other personalised features to be used by Investors to make investments and receive and manage funds in addition to monitoring and managing other matters relevant to their Investments.

2.24. **"You"**, **"your"** and **"Investors"** refers to current or potential investors of a Property.

###### 3\. GENERAL

3.1.The Platform is developed and managed by PRYPCO Blocks and provides details of each Property available for investment through the purchase of shares, each in an individual Property (the " **Shares**). PRYPCO Blocks offers Shares to potential Investors through the Platform. Through the Shares, Investors will acquire and own a proportionate share of the SPV established for each individual Property until the end of the Investment Term, subject to the terms of this Agreement.

3.2.PRYPCO Blocks will start Investment Rounds through the Platform to pool Investments from potential Investors to secure a Funding Target for the purchase of a specific Property. In exchange for the Investment, the investors will be issued a certain number/percentage of Share(s). The Funding Target will be equal to an estimated sale price of the Property agreed between PRYPCO Blocks and Seller together with associated costs incurred as a result of its acquisition through PRYPCO Blocks. PRYPCO Blocks uses the services of leading independent valuations consultants to verify the sale price of each Property. The valuer will prepare a detailed report pertaining to the Property. The details as to the Funding Target including all acquisition costs, expenses and fees will be provided on the Platform.

3.3.Subject to the terms of this Agreement, you understand to make an Investment in return for a certain number/percentage of Share(s) and that your Investment will be used for the acquisition of the Property. By subscribing to the Shares, you agree to pay proportionality all fees and charges associated with the acquisition of the Property and other related costs in connection with the Investment as set out on the Platform. Should you have any query in connection with any provisions of this Agreement and the investment procedure, you are encouraged to read through the FAQ's and if in doubt contact us through [discover.blocks@prypco.com](mailto:discover.blocks@prypco.com)

3.4.For each Property that PRYPCO Blocks achieve the Funding Target within the Investment Round, a special purpose vehicle (" **SPV**") will be established and the ownership structure behind the SPV will be changed based on each individual Property specific basis. Once the SPV has been created, you will be sent a share certificate representing your Shares.

3.5.If we fail to achieve the Funding Target within a certain period, or if the Funding Target is not lowered in agreement with the Seller, the Investment Round will be discontinued and the amount that you invested will be returned to your Customer Wallet. No costs, expenses or fees will be deducted from the amount of the Investment, except if the original funds in your Customer Wal

Virtual Asset

(VA) standards

Note:

“PRYPCO Mint” is hereby referred to as “PRYPCO FZE”

PRYPCO FZE has established a comprehensive framework of standards for the Virtual Assets (VAs) listed on its platform and for the provision of VA Broker-Dealer Services. These rigorous standards are central to maintaining a secure, transparent, and compliant trading environment. They ensure that all Virtual Assets meet stringent regulatory, technical, and market criteria both before listing and throughout their lifecycle on the platform. By implementing these standards, PRYPCO FZE upholds market integrity, protects investor interests, and fosters trust among stakeholders.

Transparency and Accessibility

PRYPCO FZE VA Standards are published on its official website to promote transparency and provide clarity to market participants, issuers, and other stakeholders. This open approach reflects PRYPCO FZE's dedication to upholding the highest ethical and regulatory benchmarks in the virtual asset ecosystem.

Design, Features, and Use Cases

- Whitepaper and Technical Review: Each VA’s whitepaper is thoroughly analysed for its technical specifications and governance mechanisms.
- Utility Validation: PRYPCO FZE examines whether the VA is achieving its intended use cases in practice.

Compliance Features

- Legal and Regulatory Adherence: Each VA is reviewed to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements, sanctions laws, intellectual property rights, and DLD.
- Risk Mitigation: Identified compliance risks are documented, with actionable recommendations provided to address any gaps. Continuous monitoring ensures ongoing alignment with legal frameworks.

Regulatory Treatment

- Jurisdictional Clarity: PRYPCO FZE consults regulatory notices, guidelines, and updates from VARA and other global authorities to determine the VA’s status.
- Proactive Engagement: If the regulatory treatment of a VA is ambiguous, PRYPCO FZE proactively engages with VARA or seeks expert legal opinions to ensure full compliance before listing.

DLT Protocol Security

- Security Audit: PRYPCO FZE conducts detailed assessments of the DLT protocol’s security features, including cryptographic standards, decentralisation, and immutability.
- Incident Response Preparedness: Regular security audits and monitoring enable PRYPCO FZE to respond promptly to any vulnerabilities or breaches, minimising potential risks to market participants.

Virtual Asset Rights

- Legal Assurance: The legal rights associated with the VA are thoroughly examined, including ownership structures, governing jurisdiction, and relevant precedents.
- Periodic Validation: Ongoing reviews ensure that rights remain enforceable and aligned with jurisdictional requirements.

Virtual Asset Availability

- Sufficient Reserves: PRYPCO FZE conducts regular audits to verify that sufficient VAs is available to meet trading and settlement obligations.
- Real-Time Monitoring: Advanced monitoring systems provide continuous updates on asset availability, ensuring operational resilience.

Alignment with Physical Markets

- Market Reflection: VAs linked to physical markets are periodically reviewed to ensure that their on-chain representations accurately reflect the underlying assets.
- Contractual Integrity: Terms and conditions are updated to remain consistent with real-world market operations.

Future Development

- Roadmap Evaluation: PRYPCO FZE reviews the VA’s development roadmap for feasibility, credibility, and alignment with stated goals.
- Milestone Monitoring: Progress against planned milestones is tracked, and significant deviations may trigger a reassessment.

Price Manipulation Risks

- Surveillance Systems: Advanced analytics are used to detect irregular trading patterns, such as wash trading or pump-and-dump schemes.
- Mitigation Strategies: Identified risks are addressed through enhanced monitoring, stricter listing conditions, or, where necessary, suspension of trading activities.

Conflict of Interest

- Ethical Governance: Potential conflicts of interest between the VA issuer and PRYPCO FZE are identified and addressed.
- Independent Audits: Third-party audits and transparency measures reinforce trust and ensure that PRYPCO FZE operations remain impartial.

Ongoing Monitoring and Dynamic Adaptation

PRYPCO FZE VA Standards are not static; they evolve in response to emerging market trends, regulatory updates, and technological advancements. This adaptive approach enables PRYPCO FZE to proactively address potential risks, maintain compliance, and uphold the integrity of its platform.

Continuous Evaluation

PRYPCO FZE conducts regular evaluations of listed VAs, applying the same rigorous standards as those used during the initial listing process. This ensures that all assets continue to meet required criteria and remain suitable for trading on the platform.

Proactive Delisting

Should a VA fail to meet the established standards or present heightened risks, PRYPCO FZE takes decisive action, which may include suspending trading, implementing enhanced monitoring, or delisting the asset altogether.

Stakeholder Communication

PRYPCO FZE remains committed to transparency by informing stakeholders about significant changes to VA listings, including delisting decisions or modifications to listing conditions. These updates are shared through official channels, ensuring that all market participants remain informed.

Collaboration with Regulators

PRYPCO FZE maintains an open line of communication with VARA and other regulatory authorities to align its practices with evolving legal and regulatory expectations. This collaboration ensures that PRYPCO FZE platform remains a leader in regulatory compliance within the virtual asset sector. By implementing and continuously refining these standards, PRYPCO FZE ensures that its platform operates with the highest levels of integrity, transparency, and compliance, creating a secure and trustworthy environment for all market participants.

# The Future of Real-World Investing. Built the Right Way.

For decades, many of the world's most compelling assets were available only to institutions and private networks. Tokinvest is changing that, responsibly, by enabling regulated, tokenised assets to real-world assets through a secure and compliant marketplace

[Explore as an Investor](https://tokinvest.capital/investors) [Tokenise an Asset](https://tokinvest.capital/asset-owner)

Granted the first multi-asset issuance license from the Dubai Virtual Assets Regulatory Authority (VARA).

Tokinvest is permitted to operate as a Virtual Asset Broker-Dealer; and to serve retail, qualified, and institutional investors in and from Dubai.

Tokinvest platform gives you access to products currently unavailable on 99.9% of existing trading platforms, making it easy for anyone to buy and sell assets digitally.

Tokinvest is permitted to operate as a Virtual Asset Broker-Dealer; and to serve retail, qualified, and institutional investors in and from Dubai.

The Tokinvest marketplace is accessible to all and simplifies the buying, selling, and management of real-world asset investments by creating virtual tokens that represent the legal ownership rights of physical assets.

# What is an RWA Token?

A Real-World Asset (RWA) token, sometimes referred to as an RWA coin, replaces traditional paper-based legal contracts with an electronic version contained inside a ‘smart contract’ on an online ledger (blockchain).

This ledger records ownership and transfer records of your legal rights to real-world assets, such as real estate, commodities, art, equities, or investment funds.

RWA tokens bring the benefits of blockchain—transparency, security, efficiency and fractionalisation—to traditional asset classes, delivering on blockchain’s promise of democratising financial products by significantly reducing the financial barrier of ownership.

[Learn more](https://tokinvest.capital/investors)

# Unleash Greater Value for Your Assets

As an asset owner, creating virtual assets with Tokinvest lets you mobilise the locked-up value of your physical asset by tokenising and allowing it to be sold as multiple tokens (fractionalisation).

![Fractional Ownership](https://tokinvest-website.cdn.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/ZvaBtbVsGrYSwERS_FractionalOwnership.svg)

## Fractional Ownership

By dividing assets into smaller, tradable tokens, you can attract more investors from broader financial demographics and geographies.

![Increased Liquidity](https://tokinvest-website.cdn.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/ZvaB3rVsGrYSwERZ_IncreasedLiquidity.svg)

## Increased Liquidity

Tokenisation allows for significantly cheaper and faster transactions, turning traditionally illiquid assets into liquid ones.

![Center Square Image](https://tokinvest.capital/_next/image?url=%2F_next%2Fstatic%2Fmedia%2FAssetsCente

# About Tokinvest

We make it easy to invest in assets that were once accessible only to the wealthiest, bringing previously unimaginable opportunities to all. Tokinvest creates and issues fractional investment products by working together with the owners of those assets, who are looking to make their asset investible to a broader market more efficiently and at a lower entry point. Tokinvest provides both the initial issuance as well as a marketplace so investors are able to buy, sell and trade seamlessly.

# Meet our team

![](https://images.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/aPHZZZ5xUNkB2E-__WhatsAppImage2025-10-08at17.20.01.jpeg?auto=format,compress)

## Scott Thiel

CEO, Founder

Scott Thiel is the CEO and founder of Tokinvest. He brings over 20 years of experience as an award-winning lawyer and entrepreneur. Scott played a key role in the advisory team that developed the VARA virtual assets regulatory framework.

Scott has been a long-term member of the Hedera LLC board and serves as a governing council representative. Additionally, he was a Senior Partner and global fintech co-chair for DLA Piper.

Read more

![](https://images.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/Zyyllq8jQArT0dZ4_mattblom.png?auto=format,compress)

## Matt Blom

CSO

Matt Blom is the CSO of Tokinvest. He is a serial entrepreneur with over 27 years of senior management experience in the financial markets across the UK, UAE, and China.

After creating one of the UK’s most successful proprietary trading companies, he went on to build a worldwide private social media app and a globally regulated Nasdaq-listed digital asset business.

Matt is an advisor to multiple technology and Web3 startups and a regular guest as a crypto market specialist on Dubai Eye, Dubai One, and CNBC Arabia. He is also a former DFSA Registered Executive Officer.

Read more

![](https://images.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/ZyymDa8jQArT0daD_robcooper.png?auto=format,compress)

## Robert Cooper

COO, CRO

Robert is the COO and CRO at Tokinvest. Previously, he was the Founder and CEO of Digivault, the first standalone custodian to be granted a custodial registration under the UK FCA’s cryptoasset regime. Boasting two decades of leadership and management experience building world class teams in the defence and fintech sectors.  Rob has successfully delivered a number of complex high value programmes for some of the world’s largest MSPs, banks and the Ministry of Defence. He is also a former Army Officer within the Commandos.

Read more

![](https://images.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/Zy3hmK8jQArT0oTX_JamesByrne.png?auto=format,compress)

## James Byrne

CTO

James Byrne is the CTO at Tokinvest. James has over two decades of experience in finance, where he has spearheaded infrastructure transformation programs at top global banks.

After founding Digivault, the first standalone crypto custodian registered with the UK regulator, James served as CTO for five years. During his tenure, he developed a leading cold and warm crypto custody solution, processing more than $3 billion.

James regularly contributes to forums, discussing blockchain’s role in traditional finance and the evolution of security tokens.

Read more

![](https://images.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/Zy3jLa8jQArT0oUY_HeatherDale.png?auto=format,compress)

## Heather Dale

Head of Marketing

Heather Dale is the Head of Marketing at Tokinvest. Heather brings almost two decades of experience of public relations, branding and content creation experience to her clients. Having started her career as a journalist at the Financial Times in London and Hong Kong, she made the leap into public relations in 2013. During the past decade, she has worked with global, regional and start-up companies across the world advising on strategic communications, media relations, crisis communications, business launches and financial communications.

Read more

![](https://images.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/Zy3iyK8jQArT0oUJ_MartinWalker.png?auto=format,compress)

## Martin Walker

Head of Talent

Martin Walker is the Head of Talent at Tokinvest. Martin Walker is a senior-level executive search professional specialising in the emerging Technology, FinTech, and Crypto sectors. With extensive experience across Asia-Pacific, the Middle East, Europe, and the US.

Over the past two decades, Martin has partnered with globally recognised growth companies, from Series A startups to Fortune 500 firms, on mission-critical hires.

Martin has also established a reputation as a keynote speaker, emerging technology evangelist, and investor.

Read more

![](https://images.prismic.io/tokinvest-website/aYH7VN0YXLCxVTov_1770065090688.jpeg?auto=format%2Ccompress&rect=131%2C0%2C939%2C1008&w=1193&h=1280)

## Umair Ahmed

CCO, MLRO

Umair Ahmed is the CCO and MLRO of Tokinvest. With more than 20 years of experience in financial crime compliance, regulatory compliance, and blockchain, Umair has held senior global and regional leadership roles across traditional financial institutions and digital asset firms.

Umair has played global compliance roles at Binance and has worked closely with Fuze Finance on VARA-led remediation and regulatory enhancement programmes. His leadership experience includes serving as Global and Regional Head of Compliance at Barclays, Deloitte, First Abu Dhabi Bank, HSBC, and the London Stock Exchange Group.

Read more

## GET TO KNOW CTRL ALT

## Leading Tokenization Infrastructure Provider

## $1.2bn+

in Assets Tokenized

Ctrl Alt is a tokenization infrastructure provider that makes it easy to turn assets into digital investments. We help our clients structure, issue and manage tokenized products, like real estate, private markets, funds and more.

We combine the power of tokenization with our expertise in financial engineering to simplify the entire investment lifecycle for alternative assets.

## Our Solutions

[For Asset Managers](https://ctrl-alt.co/#w-tabs-0-data-w-pane-0) [For Institutions](https://ctrl-alt.co/#w-tabs-0-data-w-pane-1) [For Investors](https://ctrl-alt.co/#w-tabs-0-data-w-pane-2)

![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/6864df64d1f5a690c14427f5/697a4526f43da8281d0b4f97_AdobeStock_500200923%201.png)

[Schedule a Consultation](https://ctrl-alt.co/#contact) [Learn More](https://ctrl-alt.co/for-asset-managers/distribute)

### Overview

###### Distribute

Access a wider pool of investors by using tokenization to lower minimums, offer greater choice and unlock on-chain capital.

###### Structure

For Asset Managers that operate SPVs, funds or other forms of wrappers, we offer tokenized, scalable and cost-effective structures that aim to improve margins while lowering fees for investors.

###### Invest

Gain unparalleled access to a diverse range of tokenized investment opportunities. With tokenization you can invest directly into assets that may have otherwise been difficult to access. Broaden your investment universe.

#### WHO IS THIS FOR

Asset Manager

Wealth Manager

Family Office

Boutique Investment Banks and more

### WHY TOKENIZE ASSETS?

###### Distribution

Expand your investor reach and simplify cross-sector distribution with digital assets that are faster to issue, transfer and settle.

###### Access

Give your clients access to a diverse range of alternative assets, from real estate to private markets, we can help you keep up with client demand.

###### Revenue

Bring new lines of revenue to your business in a simple, quick and cost-effective way.

###### Lead The Way

Stand out in a competitive market by offering your clients access to exclusive tokenized investment opportunities.

#### WHO IS THIS FOR

Asset Manager

Wealth Manager

Family Office

Boutique Investment Banks and more

## SOURCE: firecrawl/openai-adgm-difc-landscape.md
================================================================================

As of April 2026, the Abu Dhabi Global Market (ADGM) Financial Services Regulatory Authority (FSRA) has licensed over 20 firms to conduct activities involving Virtual Assets (VAs) or Fiat-Referenced Tokens (FRTs). ([adgm.com](https://www.adgm.com/media/announcements/adgm-fsra-presents-key-enhancements-to-its-digital-assets-framework-at-abu-dhabi-finance-week-2025?utm_source=openai)) While the FSRA does not publicly disclose a comprehensive list of these entities, the licensed firms encompass a range of services, including broker-dealers, custodians, exchanges, asset managers, and FRT issuers.

In the Dubai International Financial Centre (DIFC), the Dubai Financial Services Authority (DFSA) has established a robust regulatory framework for digital assets. This framework covers recognized crypto tokens, including fiat crypto tokens, and investment tokens. It addresses various activities such as issuance, trading on DFSA-regulated exchanges and multilateral trading facilities, holdings in digital wallets, and associated asset management activities. All firms providing financial services related to crypto tokens in or from the DIFC are required to obtain the appropriate license from the DFSA. ([difc.com](https://www.difc.com/business/areas-business/digital-assets?utm_source=openai))

In January 2026, the DFSA implemented major updates to its Crypto Token Regulatory Framework to enhance market integrity and support innovation within the DIFC. These updates reflect the DFSA's commitment to maintaining a safe, transparent, and well-regulated digital assets environment. ([dfsa.ae](https://www.dfsa.ae/news/dfsa-implements-major-updates-crypto-token-regulatory-framework-enhancing-market-integrity-and-supporting-innovation-difc?utm_source=openai))

Comparatively, the Virtual Assets Regulatory Authority (VARA) in Dubai oversees virtual asset activities outside the DIFC. VARA's regulatory framework is designed to position Dubai as a global hub for virtual assets, focusing on fostering innovation while ensuring consumer protection and market integrity.

Regarding the total number of licensed virtual asset firms across all UAE regulators, specific figures are not publicly disclosed. However, with over 20 firms licensed by the ADGM FSRA and a growing number of entities obtaining licenses from the DFSA and VARA, the UAE continues to solidify its position as a leading jurisdiction for virtual asset activities.

The firm utilizes proprietary high-frequency trading infrastructure and quantitative models to offer streaming liquidity across a broad range of tokens and fiat currencies, including USD, EUR, GBP, and AED. Recently, Selini integrated with the Talos Provider Network, enhancing access to its services for institutional clients. The company focuses on delivering private banking-grade digital wealth management services to ultra-high-net-worth individuals and leading institutions. In December 2025, Amber Premium FZE received an in-principle approval from Dubai's Virtual Assets Regulatory Authority (VARA), marking a significant step toward full authorization for virtual asset activities in the region. ([nasdaq.com](https://www.nasdaq.com/press-release/amber-premium-fze-secures-principle-approval-vara-virtual-asset-service-provider?utm_source=openai))

3. **DKK Digital FZE**: DKK Digital FZE is a Dubai-based subsidiary of DKK Partners, specializing in providing regulated, seamless, and scalable fiat-to-stablecoin infrastructure for institutions in the UAE, MENA, and beyond. The company offers services such as fiat on-ramp and off-ramp capabilities, stablecoin liquidity, and advisory support. In January 2025, DKK Digital FZE secured an in-principle approval from VARA, positioning itself as a trusted leader in stablecoins and digital finance. ([dkkdigital.io](https://dkkdigital.io/?utm_source=openai))

4. **Atremo Digital FZE**: Atremo Digital FZE is a VARA-regulated Virtual Asset Service Provider holding a Broker-Dealer Services License. The company facilitates the purchase and sale of virtual assets, operating under the regulatory framework established by VARA. ([files.atremodigital.com](https://files.atremodigital.com/purchase_and_sales_agreement.pdf?utm_source=openai))

These entities are recognized as VARA-licensed Virtual Asset Service Providers, indicating their compliance with Dubai's regulatory standards for virtual assets.

## SOURCE: analysis/interview-analysis-gpt54.md
================================================================================

Below is a structured analysis of the interview, with direct answers to Hari’s two unresolved questions and the practical implications for Antweave’s roadmap now that the target is **Broker-Dealer only** under VARA.

---

# 1. Executive takeaway from the interview

## What became clear
From the interview, the regulatory target is now much narrower and more achievable than initially assumed:

### Antweave does **not** want a Category 1 / VA Issuance setup
They do **not** want to be the regulated token issuer.

Instead, the intended model is:

- **A third-party licensed/regulated tokenization issuer** such as **Ctrl Alt** or **Tokinvest** structures and issues the real-world asset tokens
- **Antweave** acts as the **distribution / placement / brokerage layer**
- Antweave’s role is to **sell or facilitate sale/purchase of those tokens to clients/public** under a **VARA Broker-Dealer** model
- They already have a **DMCC company**, which is useful as the local corporate base for the VARA process
- They have **AED 100M+ real estate inventory** from media barter deals, which gives immediate commercial use case
- **Hari** is effectively leading the tokenization vertical internally

This is a major simplification of scope.

---

# 2. Correct regulatory framing: BD-only model

Under VARA, the key question is not “are you touching tokens?” but **what regulated VA activity are you performing?**

If Antweave:
- does not issue its own VA,
- does not run a multilateral market,
- does not operate custody for clients,
- and instead introduces, arranges, and executes token purchases/sales for clients,

then the primary license target is **Broker-Dealer Services**.

That is very different from:
- **Issuer Services**
- **Exchange Services**
- **Lending/Borrowing**
- **Custody**
- **VA Management / Advisory**

---

# 3. Hari’s Question 1  
## “What is the key difference between how Prypco facilitates secondary sales of tokens vs a VARA exchange service?”

This is the most important regulatory distinction.

---

## Short answer

A **Broker-Dealer** may facilitate secondary sales of tokens **on behalf of specific buyers and sellers**, including arranging and executing bilateral transactions.

An **Exchange** under VARA is different because it operates a **multilateral trading facility** or **market infrastructure** where:
- multiple third-party buy/sell interests interact,
- orders are brought together systematically,
- and trades are matched or executed according to platform rules, often with an order book or matching engine.

So the legal distinction is:

### Broker-Dealer
- acts as an intermediary in a **client-to-client** or **client-to-market-maker** transaction
- facilitates **bilateral** or dealer-intermediated trades
- may arrange a sale, source a counterparty, negotiate price, and execute the trade
- does **not** operate an open multilateral market

### Exchange
- operates the venue/mechanism where **multiple participants’ interests interact**
- provides **multilateral matching**
- typically uses a **trading book, matching engine, or execution protocol**
- functions like a marketplace rather than a broker

---

## VARA rulebook distinction

Under VARA’s activity-based framework, the relevant distinction is between:

### 1) Broker-Dealer Services
This activity covers persons who:
- arrange deals in virtual assets,
- solicit or accept orders,
- execute transactions for clients,
- buy/sell VAs as agent or intermediary,
- and facilitate transactions without necessarily running a market venue.

### 2) Exchange Services
This covers operation of a platform or facility that:
- brings together multiple third-party buying and selling interests,
- allows those interests to interact,
- and results in contracts or trades in virtual assets.

The key regulatory concept is **multilateral interaction**.

If the platform is simply helping A find B and then facilitating a transaction as intermediary, that is closer to **Broker-Dealer**.

If the platform creates a venue where many participants place standing interests and the system determines who trades with whom, that is **Exchange**.

---

## Why Prypco can facilitate secondary trades without being an exchange

Based on the operating model generally described publicly, Prypco’s regulated tokenized real estate setup in Dubai has been positioned around **broker-dealer style intermediation**, not a full exchange.

That means the secondary sales process is likely structured as something like this:

- token holders indicate they want to sell
- interested buyers indicate willingness to buy
- Prypco/platform facilitates the transaction
- execution happens in a controlled, brokered manner
- pricing/discovery may be guided or arranged
- settlement occurs through the approved structure
- but the platform is not presented as an open multilateral trading venue with an exchange-style order book

In other words, the platform may enable **secondary transfers**, but that alone does **not** make it an exchange.

Secondary trading is not the issue.

The issue is **how** the trading is organized.

---

## Legal distinction in practical terms

### Prypco-style BD model
Permissible if the platform:

- receives indication from seller: “I want to sell”
- identifies or introduces one or more buyers
- facilitates negotiation or acceptance
- executes transfer as agent/intermediary
- possibly works on an RFQ or brokered execution basis
- does not expose live firm orders from multiple participants into a multilateral matching environment

This is essentially **brokered secondary liquidity**.

### Exchange model
Would arise if the platform:

- displays standing bids/offers from multiple users,
- allows users to place executable orders into a common system,
- automatically or rules-based matches those orders,
- and creates a multilateral market venue.

That is closer to **Exchange Services** under VARA.

---

## The core test: bilateral vs multilateral

This is the simplest way to explain it to management.

### Broker-Dealer
“Antweave helps one client buy from another client.”

### Exchange
“Antweave operates the market where all clients’ buy/sell interests meet and are matched.”

That is the legal dividing line.

---

## Can Prypco have a platform and still remain BD?

Yes, **a platform interface itself does not make a firm an exchange**.

A broker-dealer can absolutely have:
- a client dashboard
- token listings
- offering documents
- portfolio pages
- sell requests
- buy interest forms
- indicative pricing
- bid/offer inquiry mechanisms
- matched introductions
- trade confirmation workflows

What it cannot do, without moving toward Exchange Services, is operate a **multilateral execution venue**.

So if Prypco’s platform is effectively:
- a controlled broker interface,
- not a public/open order-driven marketplace,
- and execution is intermediary-led rather than system-led,

then it can fit under BD.

---

# 4. Hari’s Question 2  
## “As a broker-dealer, are we allowed to have an automated order book? If I want to sell my token at 5 AED, you want to buy at 5 AED, an automated system matches us. Is that legal with a BD license?”

## Short answer

**Generally, no — not if it is a true automated multilateral order book that matches third-party client orders.**  
That starts to look like **Exchange Services**, not Broker-Dealer Services.

A VARA broker-dealer can facilitate trades, and may use internal systems to support execution, but once the platform is:
- receiving standing buy/sell orders from multiple users,
- maintaining an order book,
- and automatically matching those orders according to rules,

it is very likely functioning as a **multilateral trading facility / exchange-like venue**.

That would exceed a pure BD scope.

---

## Why the automated order book is the problem

The issue is not “automation” alone.

The issue is **automated multilateral interaction of trading interests**.

A BD can use systems to:
- record client instructions,
- manage internal workflow,
- send RFQs,
- route orders,
- provide indicative quotes,
- notify broker team of matching interest.

But if the system itself:
- determines execution,
- matches one client’s order with another’s,
- and does so in a continuous or rules-based way across many participants,

then the platform is no longer just assisting the broker.  
It is **operating the market**.

That is the essence of Exchange Services.

---

## Practical examples

### Likely allowed under BD
1. **Sell request board (non-executable)**
   - Seller indicates desire to sell 1,000 tokens
   - No public executable order book
   - Broker sources buyer and arranges deal manually or semi-manually

2. **RFQ system**
   - Buyer asks for quote on 1,000 tokens
   - Broker obtains or arranges quote from seller / market participant
   - Buyer accepts quote
   - Trade executed bilaterally

3. **Bulletin board**
   - Platform displays indicative opportunities
   - “Available interest in Property X tokens”
   - Interested users contact broker
   - Broker intermediates transaction

4. **Broker-assisted matching**
   - Internal system flags compatible buyer/seller interests to Antweave staff
   - Human broker confirms trade
   - No open, live, executable multilateral order book

These are generally more defensible as BD functions.

---

### Likely not allowed under BD alone
1. **Central limit order book**
   - users post bids/asks
   - platform ranks them by price/time
   - matching is automatic

2. **Continuous automated matching engine**
   - if buy = sell price, system executes without broker intervention

3. **Open marketplace with multilateral interaction**
   - all participants can see and interact with all orders
   - venue rules determine execution

4. **Exchange-style price formation**
   - platform itself becomes the trading venue for market discovery and execution

That is much more likely to be regulated as **Exchange Services**.

---

# 5. Can a BD operate a bulletin board or RFQ system w

================================================================================
## SOURCE: analysis/interview-analysis-gemini.md
================================================================================

Of course. This is a fantastic and highly specific scenario. Here is a detailed analysis covering all the points you requested.

---

### **Executive Summary**

The candidate correctly identified the startup's core strategy: a lean, fast-to-market approach using a Broker-Dealer license only and partnering for the more complex VA Issuance. However, they failed the technical stress test on the precise regulatory boundaries of that license. The interviewer, Hari, was probing for a deep understanding of *what a Broker-Dealer is not allowed to do*, which is critical for compliance. The situation is salvageable with a strong follow-up that demonstrates proactive learning and strategic application of that new knowledge. The BD-only roadmap is a significant advantage, making the path to market simpler, cheaper, and faster.

---

### **1. Detailed Answers to Hari's Questions**

These questions are designed to separate candidates with surface-level knowledge from those with a deep, functional understanding of the VARA framework.

#### **Question 1: Difference between Prypco secondary token sales vs VARA exchange service - how does Prypco do it under a BD license?**

This question is about the fundamental operational difference between a bilateral/intermediated market and a multilateral trading facility.

**The Core Distinction:**
An **Exchange Service** license is for operating a *multilateral trading facility*. The key word is **multilateral**. This is a platform, typically with a Central Limit Order Book (CLOB), that brings together *multiple* third-party buying and selling interests to interact and form contracts according to non-discretionary rules. Think of it as a public square where many people can shout their buy/sell prices, and a system automatically matches them. The exchange operator is a neutral venue provider.

A **Broker-Dealer (BD)** license is for acting as an *intermediary* in transactions. They do not operate a multilateral facility. Instead, they facilitate trades in one of two primary ways, both of which are permissible for secondary sales:

1.  **Dealing as Principal (The "Dealer" function):**
    *   **How it works:** Prypco buys the RWA token from a seller (Seller A) for its own inventory/account. At a later point, it sells that same token from its inventory to a buyer (Buyer B).
    *   **VARA Specifics:** Prypco is the direct counterparty to both Seller A and Buyer B in two separate transactions. They take on price risk by holding the token on their balance sheet, even if for a short time. They make money on the "spread" (the difference between the price they bought at and the price they sold at).
    *   **Why it's not an Exchange:** There is no direct interaction between Seller A and Buyer B. The platform is not matching third-party interests; it is acting as a market-maker.

2.  **Arranging Deals in VAs / Dealing as Agent (The "Broker" function):**
    *   **How it works:** A seller approaches Prypco wanting to sell their tokens. Prypco then actively finds a buyer for those tokens. This is often done via a "bulletin board" or "request for quote" (RFQ) system, not a live, anonymous order book. Prypco matches the buyer and seller in a "matched principal" or "agency" trade.
    *   **VARA Specifics:** Under VARA's Broker-Dealer Services Rulebook, this falls under "arranging" transactions or acting as an agent. Prypco is essentially a high-tech real estate agent for digital assets. They connect the two parties and take a commission for the service. The key is that Prypco is the central, discretionary node in the transaction.
    *   **Why it's not an Exchange:** The matching is not done by an automated, non-discretionary system open to multiple parties. Prypco is actively curating and facilitating the match. It's a high-touch, intermediated process, even if the user interface is slick.

**In summary for Hari:** Prypco facilitates secondary liquidity by acting as a classic broker-dealer. They either buy and sell for their own account (as a dealer) or actively connect a specific buyer with a specific seller (as a broker). They are legally prohibited from creating a system where multiple buyers and sellers can anonymously and automatically trade with each other, as that would constitute operating an unlicensed exchange.

---

#### **Question 2: Can a broker-dealer have an automated order book matching buyers and sellers?**

This is the technical follow-up to the first question, and the answer is a definitive no, with a crucial nuance.

**The Short Answer:** No.

**The Detailed Answer:**
An automated order book that matches buy and sell orders from multiple third parties is the *defining characteristic* of a VA Exchange under the VARA framework. If a Broker-Dealer were to implement such a system, they would be conducting Exchange Services without a license, a severe regulatory breach.

*   **VARA's Functional Approach:** VARA regulates based on the *function* being performed, not the label a company gives itself. If a platform functions like an exchange (i.e., has an automated, multilateral matching engine), VARA will regulate it as an exchange, regardless of whether the company only holds a BD license.

*   **The Nuance (What can be automated?):** A Broker-Dealer *can* use automation to make its own processes more efficient.
    *   They can have an automated client onboarding (KYC/AML) system.
    *   They can have a user interface where clients can view indicative prices and submit "requests to trade" or "indications of interest."
    *   They can use internal automated tools to scan their own inventory (principal book) or client interest lists (agency book) to find potential matches.

*   **The Critical Difference:** The automation is **internal** and **supports the broker's discretionary actions**. The final step is still a brokered transaction. For example, a client submits a "request to sell 10 tokens at 105 AED." The BD's system might flag that they have another client who has indicated interest in buying at 104 AED. A human trader at the BD firm would then intervene, perhaps calling the buyer to see if they'll come up to 105 AED, or executing a matched-principal trade. The system *assists* the broker; it does not *replace* the broker by creating a non-discretionary, multilateral market.

**In summary for Hari:** A Broker-Dealer cannot deploy an automated, multilateral order book. Doing so crosses the line into operating an exchange. However, they can and should automate their internal workflows and client-facing request systems to make their intermediation services more efficient, scalable, and user-friendly, as long as the final trade execution remains a brokered (principal or agency) transaction.

---

### **2. Assessment of How the Interview Went**

*   **The Positive:** The candidate grasped the single most important strategic insight: the company's lean, BD-only, partnership-based model. This shows good business acumen and an ability to listen and understand the core commercial strategy. This is a major point in their favor.
*   **The Negative:** The inability to answer Hari's questions is a significant red flag


================================================================================
## SOURCE: analysis/prypco-deep-research.md
================================================================================

Prypco operates as a platform facilitating the tokenization of real estate properties owned by third parties, such as developers. It does not own the properties it tokenizes. This positions Prypco as a marketplace rather than an asset originator. ([dubailand.gov.ae](https://dubailand.gov.ae/en/news-media/dld-launches-the-mena-s-first-tokenized-real-estate-project-through-the-prypco-mint-platform?utm_source=openai))

Ctrl Alt Solutions DMCC serves as the tokenization infrastructure provider for the Dubai Land Department's (DLD) Real Estate Tokenization Project. Prypco utilizes this infrastructure to offer tokenized real estate investments through its platform. Ctrl Alt is responsible for minting and issuing the title deed ownership tokens, while Prypco provides the marketplace for investors to purchase these tokens. ([ctrl-alt.co](https://www.ctrl-alt.co/press-releases/ctrl-alt-and-dubai-land-department-go-live-with-tokenized-real-estate?utm_source=openai))

The Dubai Land Department (DLD) acts as both a regulator and a partner in the real estate tokenization initiative. DLD oversees the regulatory framework and ensures compliance, while also collaborating with entities like Prypco and Ctrl Alt to implement the tokenization process. DLD issues the property title deeds, which are then tokenized and made available for investment through platforms like Prypco. ([dubailand.gov.ae](https://dubailand.gov.ae/en/news-media/dld-launches-the-mena-s-first-tokenized-real-estate-project-through-the-prypco-mint-platform?utm_source=openai))

Prypco's tokenization model involves direct ownership of property tokens backed by certificates issued by the DLD. Investors receive a certificate of ownership in their name, representing their fractional ownership of the property. This approach does not involve the use of Special Purpose Vehicles (SPVs); instead, it provides direct ownership of the tokenized property shares. ([blogs.prypco.com](https://blogs.prypco.com/ar/what-is-real-estate-tokenization-a-comprehensive-guide/?utm_source=openai))

Prypco's business model includes earning fees from transactions on its platform. While specific fee structures are not detailed in the available sources, it is common for such platforms to charge a percentage of each transaction or earn from spreads on secondary trading. For precise fee information, it would be advisable to consult Prypco's official resources or contact them directly.

Several press releases and news articles from 2025 to 2026 detail the collaboration between Prypco, Ctrl Alt, and the DLD. Notably, in May 2025, the DLD launched the region's first tokenized real estate investment project through the Prypco Mint platform, in partnership with Prypco and Ctrl Alt. This initiative marked a significant step in real estate tokenization in Dubai. ([dubailand.gov.ae](https://dubailand.gov.ae/en/news-media/dld-launches-the-mena-s-first-tokenized-real-estate-project-through-the-prypco-mint-platform?utm_source=openai))

In summary, Prypco functions as a marketplace for tokenized real estate, collaborating with Ctrl Alt for tokenization infrastructure and the DLD for regulatory oversight and property registration. Investors gain direct ownership of property tokens, with the DLD issuing certificates of ownership. Prypco's revenue model likely involves transaction-based fees, though specific details are not publicly disclosed.
